Possession Required in Sarf Even for Coined Goods
Refuting objection that coined goods require no possession in sarf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school requires possession (taqabud) in sarf for coined gold and silver items, and distinguish between actual riba and the suspicion of riba as a legal basis.

Core Idea
Even specific gold items require hand-to-hand exchange because their thaman nature creates a suspicion of riba.

This passage addresses an objection: if coined goods are specific and identifiable, why require possession? The Hanafi response reveals a key principle — the suspicion of riba (shubhat al-riba) is treated like actual riba. This lesson unpacks that principle and its application to sarf transactions.

Guided Path
1
State the objection
Identify the hypothetical argument that coined goods (muswagh) should not require possession because they become specific upon specification, unlike struck coins (madrub) which are fungible.
The objection claims that the defect of bay' al-ka'i bi al-ka'i (selling debt for debt) does not arise in specific items.
2
Identify the Hanafi ruling
Recognize that the Hanafi school rules possession as wajib in all sarf transactions involving gold and silver, regardless of whether the items are struck coins or coined goods.
3
Find the proof (qiyas)
Understand the analogy: just as actual riba is prohibited, its suspicion (shubhat al-riba) is also prohibited. Coined goods retain the nature of thaman (price), hence fall under the same ruling.
The proof is based on qiyas (analogical reasoning) and not directly on nass.
4
Understand the principle of shubhat al-riba
Grasp that the Hanafi school blocks the means to riba by considering any resemblance to riba as equally prohibited. This is a form of sadd al-dhara'i' (blocking the means).
This principle is stronger than the mere fact of specificity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و لانه ان كان يتعين ففيه .... الخ سے ایک اعتراض کا جواب ہے۔ اعتراض یہ ہے کہ بغیر قبضہ کے مضروب کی بیع مضروب کے عوض اسلئے میچ نہیں ہے کہ اس میں بیع الکائی با لکائی لازم آتا ہے لیکن مصوغ یعنی ڈھالی ہوئی چیز کو ڈھالی ہوئی چیز کے عوض بغیر قبضہ کے فروخت کرنے میں یہ خرابی لازم نہیں آتی کیونکہ ڈھائی ہوئی چیز متعین کرنے سے متعین ہو جاتی ہے۔ پس بیع المضروب بالمضروب کی صورت میں توسیع کو کالی با لکائی سے خارج کرنے کے نئے اور مساوات کو پیدا نے کیلئے دونوں عوضوں پر قبضہ کرنا ضروری ہے لیکن بین المصوغ بالمصوغ میں چونکہ یہ خرابی لازم نہیں آتی اسلئے اس صورت میں قبضہ ضروری نہ ہونا چاہیے۔
جواب ... اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ سونے اور چاندی سے ڈھالی ہوئی چیز برتن، زیور وغیرہ اگر چہ متعین کرنے سے متعین ہو جاتی ہے۔ لیکن اس کے باوجود اس میں معین نہ ہونے کا شبہ ہے کیونکہ یہ عوض پیدائشی طور پر شمن ہے یعنی اصل میں سونا چاندی ہے تو اس پر بھی قبضہ کرنا شرط ہوگا کیونکہ رہا اور سود میں جس طرح حقیقت ربوا معتبر ہے یعنی حقیقت ربوا حرام ہے اسی طرح شہبتہ الر ہوا بھی معتبر ہے یعنی شبہۃ الر ہوا بھی حرام ہے۔
And because if it becomes determined... [objection]: The sale of struck coin for struck coin without possession is not permitted because it requires bay' al-ka'i bi al-ka'i. But in the case of coined goods (muswagh), this defect does not arise because coined goods become specific when specified. So in the sale of struck for struck, to avoid bay' al-ka'i and to create equality, possession of both countervalues is necessary. But in the sale of coined for coined, since this defect does not arise, possession should not be necessary. ... The answer: Gold and silver items like utensils and jewelry, even if they become specific through specification, still have the suspicion of non-specification because they are inherently price (thaman). So possession is also required for them because, in riba, just as the reality of riba is considered (i.e., actual riba is haram), similarly the suspicion of riba is also considered (i.e., shubhat al-riba is also haram).
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, expanding on an objection to a ruling in the matn. The objection states that for struck coins (madrub), possession is required before separation to avoid bay' al-ka'i bi al-ka'i (selling debt for debt). But for coined goods (muswagh) like jewelry, since they are specific, the same defect does not arise, so possession should not be necessary. The commentator refutes this by explaining that even though the item is physically specific, gold and silver retain their essential nature as thaman (price). Therefore, the suspicion of riba (shubhat al-riba) remains, and since the suspicion of riba is treated like actual riba in the Hanafi school, possession is required. This is based on the principle that anything that leads to riba is prohibited.

Key Terms
مضروب (madrub): Struck coin, i.e., minted gold or silver coins that are not specific (they are counted by number not weight, though weight matters in riba).
مصوغ (muswagh): Coined goods, such as jewelry or utensils, that are specific and made from gold or silver.
شبهة الربا (shubhat al-riba): A situation that resembles riba, even if not actual riba, and is therefore prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is possession (taqabud) required in the sale of coined gold items (muswagh) for silver?
A) Because they are not specific and are considered debt.
B) Because they have the suspicion of riba due to their thaman nature.
C) Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) specifically prohibited it.
D) Because they are like food items.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the suspicion of riba is treated like actual riba, so possession is required in all sarf transactions involving gold and silver, including coined and jewelry items.

Meaning of Iftiraq in Sarf: Physical Separation
Defining iftiraq in sarf as physical separation with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of iftiraq in sarf contracts and distinguish it from the definition used in khiyar al-mukhayyarah.

Core Idea
In sarf, separation means physical parting – only iftiraq bi'l-abdan invalidates the contract before possession.

This lesson clarifies a key condition for the validity of sarf (currency exchange) contracts in Hanafi fiqh. The classical texts define 'iftiraq' as physical separation of the parties, not merely leaving the council. We will explore the evidence from Abdullah ibn Umar (ra) and contrast this with the ruling for a wife's option in divorce, where aversion (i'rad) rather than physical separation is decisive.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
What does 'iftiraq' mean in the context of sarf? The matn says 'before separation' (qabl al-iftiraq). The commentator clarifies it means physical separation (iftiraq bi'l-abdan).
2
Locate the evidence
Find the statement of Abdullah ibn Umar (ra) and understand its rationale. He instructs to follow the companion even if he jumps off a roof, to prevent physical separation before possession.
The dalil is a Qawl Sahabi, which is a valid proof in Hanafi usul.
3
Apply examples
Consider cases where physical separation does or does not occur: both walking together, both sleeping, both fainting. In these, the contract remains valid because physical separation has not occurred.
4
Distinguish from khiyar al-mukhayyarah
In the wife's option, when she stands up or busies herself, her option is invalidated by i'rad (aversion) even if physical separation has not occurred. This highlights that legal definitions are context-dependent.
The effective cause (illah) in each ruling differs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا ہے کہ متن میں مذکور قبل الافتراق میں افتراق سے افتراق بالا بدان مراد ہے۔ یعنی عاقدین کا اپنے بدن کے ساتھ جدا ہونا مراد ہے۔ چنانچہ عاقدین اگر مجلس عقد سے اٹھ کر دونوں ایک سمت میں چل دیے یا دونوں مجلس عقد میں سو گئے یا دونوں پر بے ہوشی طاری ہوگئی تو ان صورتوں میں چونکہ افتراق بالا بدان نہیں پایا گیا اسلئے مذکورہ تینوں صورتوں میں عقد صرف باطل نہ ہوگا۔ اس کی تائید جان شار رسول صاحبزادہ عمر فارق حضرت عبد اللہ بن عمر بن الخطاب رضی اللہ عنہما کے قول سے بھی ہوتی ہے۔ مبسوط کے حوالہ سے علامہ ابن الہمام نے پورا واقعہ اس طرح ذکر کیا ہے۔
عن ابي جبله قال سألت عبد الله بن عمر فقلت انا نقدم ارض الشام و معنا الورق الشقالي النافقه و عندهم الورق الخفاف المكاسده فنتباع ورقه العشرة بتسعة و نصف فقال لا تفعل و لكن بع ورقک بذهب و اشتر ورقهم بالذهب ولا تفارقه حتى تستوفى وان وثب عن سطح فتب معه - ابو جبلہ کہتے ہیں کہ میں نے عبداللہ بن عمر سے سوال کیا اور کہا کہ ہم لوگ ملک شام میں جارہے ہیں اور ہمارے پاس جو چاندی ہے وہ وزن میں بھاری بھی ہے اور رائج الوقت بھی ہے اور ان کے پاس جو چاندی ہے وہ ہلکی بھی ہے اور بازار میں اس کا رواج بھی ٹھپ ہے تو کیا ہم لوگ ان کی چاندی کے دس حصوں کو ساڑھے نو حصوں کے عوض خرید لیں۔ ابن عمر نے کہا یہ مت کرنا لیکن اپنی چاندی سونے کے عوض بیچ اور ان کی چاندی سونے کے عوض خرید اور اس سے جدا نہ ہونا یہاں تک کہ (اپنا حق ) وصول کرلے اور اگر وہ چھت سے کود جائے تو اس کے ساتھ تو بھی کو دجا۔ اس واقعہ سے چند باتیں معلوم ہوئیں۔ ایک تو یہ کہ چاندی اگر چاندی کے عوض فروخت کی جائے تو اس میں کمی زیادتی جائز نہیں ہے۔ لیکن اگر چاندی اور سونے میں لین دین کیا گیا تو کمی زیادتی جائز ہے۔ دوسری بات یہ معلوم ہوئی کہ عوضین پر قبضہ کئے بغیر جدانہ ہو۔ تیسری بات یہ معلوم ہوئی کہ افتراق سے مراد افتراق بالا بدان ہے۔ کیونکہ عبد اللہ بن عمرؓ نے فرمایا کہ اگر قبضہ سے پہلے تیرا ساتھی چھت سے اس لئے کو د جائے تا کہ افتراق بالا بد ان ہو کر عقد صرف باطل ہو تو تو بھی اس کے ساتھ ساتھ کو دجاتا کہ افتراق بالا بڈان ہو کر عتقد صرف باطل نہ ہو ۔ بہر حال یہ قول اس بات پر دلالت کرتا ہے کہ افتراق سے مراد افتراق بالا بدان ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ یہ جو کہا گیا کہ عقد سلم کی صورت میں افتراق سے پہلے راس المال پر قبضہ کرنا ضروری ہے تو یہاں بھی افتراق بالا بد ان ہی مراد ہے۔ اس کے بر خلاف اگر شوہر نے اپنی بیوی کو امر طلاق کا اختیار دیا اور وہ مجلس سے کھڑی ہوگئی یا اپنے شوہر کے ساتھ اسی سمت میں چلنے لگی جس طرف وہ جارہا ہے یا دوسرے کام میں مشغول ہو گئی تو اس کا اختیار باطل ہو جائے گا۔ اگر چہ تفرق بالا بدان نہ پایا جائے۔ کیونکہ منیر بعورت کا اختیار اعراض سے باطل ہو جاتا ہے اور مذکورہ صورتوں میں اعراض موجود ہے۔ اسلئے ان صورتوں میں مخیرہ کا اختیار باطل ہو جائے گا اگر چہ تفرق بالا بدان نہیں پایا گیا۔ حاصل یہ کہ خیار مخیرہ میں اعراض معتبر ہے نہ کہ تفرق بالا بدان۔ اور عقد صرف کے عوضین اور راس المال پر قبضہ کرنے میں تفرق بالا بدان معتبر ہے۔ یعنی تفرق بالا بد ان سے پہلے قبضہ درست ہے۔ اور تفرق بالا بد ان کے بعد درست نہ ہوگا۔
The author of al-Hidayah said: In the matn, 'before separation' (qabl al-iftiraq) means separation by bodies (iftiraq bi'l-abdan), i.e., the contracting parties physically parting. So if the contracting parties stand up from the council and both walk away, or both fall asleep in the council, or both become unconscious, then since physical separation has not occurred, the sarf contract does not become invalid in these three cases. This is supported by the statement of Sayyiduna Abdullah ibn Umar ibn al-Khattab (may Allah be pleased with them both). From al-Mabsut, Imam Ibn al-Humam narrated the whole incident as follows: From Abu Jablah: I asked Abdullah ibn Umar, saying: We go to the land of Sham and we have heavy, circulated silver coins, and they have light, non-circulated coins. Can we buy ten of their coins for nine and a half of ours? He said: Do not do that. But sell your silver for gold, then buy their silver with gold, and do not separate from him until you receive (your right). If he jumps off the roof, jump with him. ... Several things are learned from this incident: First, that selling silver for silver with increase or decrease is not permissible. But if silver and gold are exchanged, increase is permissible. Second, that one must not separate without possession of both countervalues. Third, that separation (iftiraq) means physical separation, because Abdullah ibn Umar said: If your companion jumps off the roof to cause physical separation and thus invalidate the sarf contract, you should jump with him so that physical separation does not occur and the contract is not invalidated. In any case, this statement indicates that separation means physical separation. The author of al-Hidayah says: It is also stated that in the case of salam, possession of the capital before separation is necessary, and here too separation means physical separation. On the contrary, if a husband gives his wife authority in the matter of divorce, and she stands up from the council, or starts walking with her husband in the same direction, or busies herself with another matter, then her option becomes invalid, even if physical separation has not occurred. Because a woman's option (khiyar) becomes invalid due to aversion (i'rad), and in these cases aversion exists. Therefore, in these cases, the khiyar of the mukhayyarah becomes invalid even if physical separation has not occurred. The conclusion is that in khiyar al-mukhayyarah, aversion is considered, not physical separation. In the possession of countervalues in sarf and the capital (in salam), physical separation is considered. That is, possession before physical separation is valid; after physical separation it is not valid.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling passage. It clarifies that the term 'iftiraq' (separation) in the matn of al-Hidayah regarding sarf means physical separation (iftiraq bi'l-abdan) — when the two parties physically part ways. The commentator, expanding on the matn, explains three scenarios where physical separation does not occur: (1) both stand and walk together, (2) both fall asleep in the council, (3) both become unconscious. In these cases, the contract remains valid. The author then provides evidence from the statement of Ibn Umar (ra), who ordered a companion to follow his counterpart both in possession and in physical movement to avoid invalidation. The text also contrasts sarf with the case of khiyar al-mukhayyarah (option given to a wife in divorce), where aversion (i'rad) rather than physical separation nullifies the option. This highlights that legal definitions are context-dependent within Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
افتراق بالبدن (iftiraq bi'l-abdan): Physical separation of the two contracting parties' bodies, which is the condition for the invalidity of a sarf contract if possession has not occurred.
اختیار مخیرہ (ikhtiyar mukhayyarah): The option given to a woman in the matter of divorce where her acceptance or rejection is required within the council.
اعراض (i'rad): Aversion or turning away, used here to indicate that the woman's disengagement from the option nullifies it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if both parties stand up and walk away together from the council before taking possession in a sarf contract?
A) The contract becomes batil because they have separated.
B) The contract remains valid because physical separation has not occurred.
C) The contract becomes fasid because possession is missing.
D) The contract is suspended until they return.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, 'iftiraq' in sarf contracts means physical separation (iftiraq bi'l-abdan); possession before that separation is a condition for validity; this differs from khiyar al-mukhayyarah where aversion invalidates.

Gold for Silver: Tafadul Permitted, Taqabud Obligatory
Ruling with proof on gold-silver exchange (sarf)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on exchanging gold for silver, including the permissibility of tafadul, the obligation of taqabud, and the invalidity of khiyar and ajal.

Core Idea
In sarf, unequal amounts are allowed but hand-to-hand delivery is wajib; conditions delaying possession invalidate the contract.

Gold and silver are different genera in Hanafi law, so exchanging them in unequal amounts is free from riba al-fadl. However, the hadith 'gold for silver is riba except hand to hand' imposes a strict requirement of immediate mutual possession. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof, and the consequences of stipulating options or deferments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a sale of gold for silver (sarf). Determine the hukm for tafadul (unequal amounts) and taqabud (hand-to-hand).
Tafadul is permitted; taqabud is wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: the hadith 'الذهب بالورق ربا إلا هاء وهاء'. Note its type (Sunnah ahad) and authority.
The exception 'illa haa' wa haa' makes immediate exchange the only permissible form.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith proves the obligation of hand-to-hand possession and why tafadul is not prohibited (different jins).
Riba al-fadl applies only within the same genus.
4
Analyse the conditions for validity
Identify the requirements for a valid sarf: taqabud in the council, no khiyar, no ajal. Explain the consequence of iftiraq before possession (batil).
The contract is batil if parties separate before full possession.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Zufar disagrees on the revival of the contract when khiyar is dropped in the council. State the majority position.
The majority holds the contract revives once the option is dropped before the council ends.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان باع الذهب بالفضة جاز التفاضل لعدم المجانسة ووجب التقابض لقوله عليه السلام الذهب بالورق بوا الاهاء وهاء فان افتر قافى الصرف قبل العوضين او احدهما بطل العقد لفوات الشرط وهو القبض ولهذا لا يصح شرط الخيار فيه ولا الاجل لان باحدهما لايبقى القبض مستحقاو بالثاني يفوت القبض المستحق الا اذا اسقط الخيار في المجلس فيعود الى الجواز لا رتفاعه قبل تقرره وفيه خلاف زفر
ترجمہ اور اگر سونا، چاندی کے عوض بیچا تو کمی ، زیادتی جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ دونوں ایک جنس نہیں ہیں۔ اور مجلس میں باہمی قبضہ واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ سونا چاندی کے عوض سود ہے مگر ہاتھ دور ہاتھ ۔ پھر اگر عاقدین ، عقد صرف میں عوضین پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے یا ایک عوض پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے جدا ہو گئے تو عقد باطل ہو جائے گا کیونکہ شرط یعنی قبضہ فوت ہو گیا ہے اور اسی وجہ سے عقد صرف میں خیار کی شرط لگانا صحیح نہیں ہے اور نہ میعاد کی شرط لگانا ریح ہے)۔ کیونکہ ان دونوں میں سے ایک سے قبضہ کا استحقاق نہیں رہتا ہے اور ثانی سے قبضہ کا استحقاق فوت ہو جاتا ہے۔ لیکن اگر مجلس میں خیار ساقط کر دیا گیا تو عقد جائز ہو کر عود کرے گا۔ کیونکہ فساد مستحکم ہونے سے پہلے مرتفع ہو گیا ہے اور اس میں امام زفر کا اختلاف ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر سونا، چاندی کے عوض بیچا گیا تو ان میں تفاضل یعنی ایک کا کم ہونا اور ایک کا زائد ہونا جائز ہے اور وجہ جواز اتحاد جنس کا موجود نہ ہوتا ہے۔ کیونکہ اتحاد جنس موجود نہ ہونے کی صورت میں کمی ، زیادتی کے ساتھ فروخت کرنا جائز ہوتا ہے۔ البتہ مجلس عقد میں دونوں عوضوں پر باہمی قبضہ کرنا واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ اللہ کے پاک رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ سونے کو چاندی کے عوض بیچنا ہوا ہے یعنی حرام ہے مگر لے اور لا کے ساتھ یعنی ہاتھ درہاتھ جائز ہے اور اگر عقد صرف میں عوضین یا احد العوضین پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے عاقدین جدا ہو گئے تو عقد صرف باطل ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ عقد صرف کے بیچ ہونے کو باقی رکھنے کیلئے جو شرط تھی یعنی عوضین پر قبضہ کر نا وہ شرط چونکہ فوت ہو گئی ہے اسلئے عقد صرف باطل ہو جائے گا اور چونکہ بغیر قبضہ کئے مجلس سے عاقدین کا جدا ہونا عقد صرف کو باطل کر دیتا ہے اسلئے عقد صرف میں نہ خیار کی شرط لگانا صحیح ہے اور نہ میعاد کی شرط لگانا صحیح ہے۔ خیار کی صورت تو یہ ہے کہ احد العاقدین نے کہا کہ میں نے ان دنانیہ کو ان دراہم کے عوض اس شرط پر خریدا کہ مجھے کو تین دن کا اختیار ہے اور میعاد کی صورت یہ ہے کہ میں نے ان دنا نیر کو ان دراہم کے
And if he sold gold for silver, then disparity is permitted due to lack of homogeneity, and hand-to-hand exchange is obligatory because of his (peace be upon him) statement: 'Gold for silver is riba except hand to hand.' So if they separate in sarf before possession of both countervalues or one of them, the contract becomes invalid because the condition (possession) has been lost. Therefore, stipulation of the option (khiyar) or a term (ajal) is not valid in it, because by one of them, possession does not remain obligatory, and by the second, the obligatory possession is lost. Except if the option is dropped in the council, then it reverts to permissibility because the corruption was lifted before it became established. And in this there is a disagreement with Zufar. Translation: And if gold is sold for silver, then increase and decrease are permitted because they are not of the same genus. And mutual possession in the council is obligatory because the Holy Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Gold for silver is riba except hand to hand.' Then if the parties separate in a sarf contract before possession of both countervalues or one of them, the contract becomes invalid because the condition, i.e., possession, has been lost. For this reason, stipulating an option or a term in sarf is not valid. Because by one of them, the right to possession does not remain, and by the second, the right to possession is lost. But if the option is dropped in the council, the contract becomes permissible because the corruption was removed before it became established. And in this there is a disagreement with Imam Zufar. Elaboration: The scenario is that if gold is sold for silver, then disparity (one less, the other more) is permitted, and the reason is that homogeneity is not present. Because when homogeneity is absent, selling with increase or decrease is permissible. However, mutual possession in the council is obligatory. Because Allah's pure Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Selling gold for silver is riba i.e., forbidden, except with take and give (hand to hand).' And if the parties in a sarf contract separate before possession of both countervalues or one countervalue, then the sarf contract becomes invalid. Because the condition for maintaining the sarf contract, i.e., possession, has been lost. And since separation from council without possession invalidates the sarf contract, therefore, stipulating an option or a term in sarf is not correct. The option scenario: one of the parties says: I have bought these dinars for these dirhams on condition that I have an option for three days. The term scenario: I have bought these dinars for these dirhams... [text ends]
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the author of al-Hidayah, expanding on the matn regarding the sale of gold for silver. It states the key Hanafi positions: (1) Tafadul (unequal exchange) is permitted because gold and silver are different genera (jins) — thus the prohibition of riba al-fadl does not apply. (2) Taqabud (hand-to-hand possession) is wajib in the same council, based on the hadith: 'Gold for silver is riba except hand to hand.' (3) If the parties separate (iftiraq bi'l-abdan) before complete possession, the sarf contract becomes batil (void). (4) Hence, stipulating khiyar (option to rescind) or ajal (deferred payment) is not valid because they prevent immediate possession. (5) An exception: if the option is dropped in the council before the contract is finalized, the contract becomes valid again. (6) There is a disagreement with Imam Zufar on this exception. The commentary then elaborates on the meaning of the hadith and the reasoning behind the invalidity of khiyar and ajal, giving examples of how these conditions are phrased. This passage covers a complete legal unit: the ruling, its proof, its conditions, and an intra-madhhab dispute.

Key Terms
تفاضل (tafadul): Unequal exchange, e.g., giving 10 grams of gold for 20 grams of silver, which is permitted due to different genera.
تقابض (taqabud): Hand-to-hand possession, both parties taking possession in the same council before separation.
شرط خیار (shart khiyar): Condition of a stipulated option to rescind the contract within a period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is stipulating a deferred payment (ajal) invalid in a sarf contract for gold-silver exchange?
A) Because it causes lack of homogeneity.
B) Because it prevents the obligation of hand-to-hand possession from being fulfilled.
C) Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) specifically forbade deferred payment.
D) Because it is like a loan with interest.

Key Takeaway
In a sarf contract, unequal amounts of gold and silver are permitted, but mutual hand-to-hand possession in the council is obligatory; any condition that delays possession (khiyar, ajal) invalidates the contract, unless the condition is removed before the council ends.

Types of Kafalah and Validity of Kafalah bi al-Nafs
Definition of two types of kafalah and Hanafi proof for kafalah bi al-nafs against Shafi'i objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school validates kafalah bi al-nafs and identify the Shafi'i counter-argument along with the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
Kafalah bi al-nafs is valid because the guarantor can ensure the person's presence via indirect means, and the hadith 'al-za'eem gharim' covers it.

This lesson presents a foundational inter-madhhab dispute in the contract of kafalah (suretyship). The Hanafi school holds that a person can guarantee the physical presence of another (kafalah bi al-nafs), while a weak opinion of Imam al-Shafi'i rejects this. Understanding the arguments involved will deepen your appreciation of how Hanafi jurists combine textual proof (hadith) and practical reasoning (istiḥsān).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school rules regarding kafalah bi al-nafs. Look for the explicit statement in the text that it is permissible (ja'iz) and what is guaranteed.
The text says: 'الكفالة بالنفس جائزة والمضمون بها احضار المكفول به'.
2
Identify the opposition
Who disagrees with the Hanafi position? What is their reasoning? Find the Shafi'i objection in the passage.
Imam al-Shafi'i is quoted: 'لا يجوز لانه كفل بما لا يقدر على تسليمه'.
3
Analyze the opposing proof
Why does the opposing school consider kafalah bi al-nafs invalid? They argue that the guarantor cannot deliver what he does not control.
The Shafi'i view uses an analogy to kafalah bi al-mal, where the guarantor controls his own property.
4
Examine the Hanafi response
List the three Hanafi proofs: the hadith 'al-za'eem gharim', the possibility of indirect delivery, and the need and feasibility of realizing the meaning of kafalah.
The text gives: قوله عليه السلام الزعيم غارم, and ability to deliver by informing location or court aid, and الحاجة ماسة.
5
Determine the practical outcome
What is the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) between the two positions? Identify which position is the mufta bihi.
Hanafis allow suretyship for court appearance; the weak Shafi'i view would not. The Hanafi view is relied upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الكفالة ضربان كفالة بالنفس وكفالة بالمال فالكفالة بالنفس جائزة والمضمون بها احضار المكفول به و قال الشافعى لا يجوز لانه كفل بما لا يقدر على تسليمه اذ لا قدرة له على نفس المكفول به بخلاف الكفالة بالمال لان له ولاية على مال نفسه ولنا قوله عليه السلام الزعيم غارم وهذا يفيد مشروعية الكفالة بنوعيها ولانه يقدر على تسليمه بطريقه بان يعلم الطالب مكانه فيخلی بینه و بینه او يستعين باعوان القاضي في ذلك والحاجة ماسة اليه وقد امكن تحقيق معنى الكفالة فيه وهو الضم في المطالبة
He said: Kafalah is of two types: kafalah for the person and kafalah for property. Kafalah for the person is permissible, and what is guaranteed by it is the presentation of the person for whom the guarantee is made. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible because he guaranteed something he is unable to deliver, since he has no power over the person of the guaranteed one, unlike kafalah for property because he has authority over his own property. Our proof is his statement, peace be upon him: 'The guarantor is liable,' and this indicates the legality of both types of kafalah; and because he is able to deliver him by means of informing the claimant of his location, thus making him available, or by seeking the assistance of the judge's aides in that. And there is a pressing need for it, and it is possible to realize the meaning of kafalah in it, which is joining in the claim.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the validity of kafalah bi al-nafs (suretyship for the person). The author first states the Hanafi position: kafalah bi al-nafs is permissible, and what is guaranteed is the presentation of the person (mukful bihi). Imam al-Shafi'i's objection is presented: he argues it is invalid because the guarantor cannot deliver the person—the guaranteed person is free and not under the guarantor's control—unlike kafalah bi al-mal (suretyship for property) where the guarantor has authority over his own property. The Hanafi response is then given: first, the hadith 'al-za'eem gharim' (the guarantor is liable) is general and covers both types. Second, the guarantor is able to deliver the person by informing the claimant of his whereabouts or by using court officials. Third, there is a practical need for this type of kafalah, and the essential meaning of kafalah—joining the guarantor's responsibility to that of the principal—is realized here. Thus, the Hanafi position is established as correct.

Key Terms
الكفالة بالنفس (al-kafalah bi al-nafs): A contract where the guarantor (kafil) undertakes to present the person of the principal debtor (mukful bihi) to the creditor (mukful lahu).
الكفالة بالمال (al-kafalah bi al-mal): A contract where the guarantor undertakes to pay a debt or deliver property if the principal debtor fails.
الزعيم غارم (al-za'eem gharim): A prophetic hadith meaning 'the guarantor is liable' – used as evidence for the validity of both types of kafalah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the primary evidence for the validity of kafalah bi al-nafs?
A) Analogy (qiyas) to kafalah bi al-mal
B) The hadith 'al-za'eem gharim'
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) Necessity alone

Key Takeaway
Kafalah bi al-nafs is valid in the Hanafi school, supported by the hadith 'al-za'eem gharim' and the possibility of indirect delivery.

Valid and Invalid Wordings for Kafalah bi al-Nafs
Lists valid and invalid wordings for kafalah bi al-nafs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which wordings validly conclude a kafalah bi al-nafs contract and distinguish valid from invalid according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
In kafalah bi al-nafs, valid wordings must refer to the whole person; limb-specific terms are invalid.

Kafalah bi al-nafs is a surety contract where the guarantor is responsible for the person's presence. The wording used to conclude it is crucial. This passage from the Hidayah clarifies which expressions are valid and which are not, building on the principle that the wording must encompass the entire person, not just a part.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Contract
Recognize that this passage deals with kafalah bi al-nafs, a guarantee of a person's appearance.
2
List Valid Expressions
From the text, list the expressions that validly conclude kafalah: nafs, raqabah, ruh, jasad, ra's, badan, wajh, and even half, third, or part.
These all refer to the entire person, literally or customarily.
3
Understand the Rationale
Each valid expression indicates the whole body. The analogy to divorce shows consistency in Hanafi jurisprudence.
Mentioning a part (half, third) is valid because the person is indivisible in kafalah.
4
Identify Invalid Expressions
Expressions like 'hand' (yad) or 'foot' (rijl) are invalid because they do not represent the whole person.
These limbs cannot be used in divorce either, showing a consistent legal principle.
5
Apply the Rule
When encountering any wording for kafalah, ask: does this word normally refer to the entire person? If yes, it is valid; if it specifies a limb, it is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال: وتنعقد إذا قال تكفلت بنفس فلان او برقبته او بروحه او بجسده او برأسه وكذا ببدنه وبوجهه لان هذه الالفاظ يعبر بها عن البدن اما حقيقة اوعرفا على مامر فى الطلاق وكذا اذا قال بنصفه او بثلثه او بجزء منه لان النفس الواحدة فى حق الكفالة لاتتجزى فكان ذكر بعضها شائعا كذكر كلها بخلاف ما اذا قال تكفلت بید فلان او برجله لانه لا يعبر بهما عن البدن حتى لا يصح اضافة الطلاق اليهما وفيما تقدم يصح
He said: And it (kafalah) is concluded when he says: 'I guarantee the person of so-and-so' or 'his neck' or 'his soul' or 'his body' or 'his head' and likewise 'his body' and 'his face', because these expressions refer to the entire body, either literally or customarily, as has preceded in the chapter on divorce. Likewise, if he says: 'his half' or 'his third' or 'a part of him', because the single person is not divisible in respect of kafalah, so mentioning a part that is undifferentiated is like mentioning the whole. Contrary to when he says: 'I guarantee the hand of so-and-so' or 'his foot', because these two do not refer to the body, such that divorce cannot be attributed to them; whereas in the preceding (cases) it is valid.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the wording that validly concludes a kafalah bi al-nafs contract. The author, following the matn, enumerates valid expressions: nafs (person), raqabah (neck), ruh (soul), jasad (body), ra's (head), badan (body), wajh (face). These all refer to the entire person either literally or by custom, as previously established in the chapter on divorce. Additionally, if one says 'half', 'third', or 'part' of the person, it is also valid because the person is indivisible for the purpose of kafalah—mentioning a part implies the whole. However, if one says 'hand' or 'foot', it is invalid because these limbs do not represent the whole body; as in divorce, attributing divorce to a limb is not valid. The principle is that the wording must indicate the entire person, not a specific limb.

Key Terms
نفس (nafs): The person or self; used as a valid expression for kafalah bi al-nafs.
رقبة (raqabah): Literally 'neck', used metonymically for the whole person in kafalah.
روح (ruh): Soul or spirit; another valid expression for the entire person.
جسد (jasad): Body; a clear reference to the whole physical form.
يد (yad): Hand; an invalid expression because it does not refer to the whole body.
رجل (rijl): Foot; an invalid expression, similar to 'yad'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following expressions does NOT validly conclude a kafalah bi al-nafs according to the Hanafi school?
A) 'I guarantee his neck (raqabah)'
B) 'I guarantee his head (ra's)'
C) 'I guarantee his hand (yad)'
D) 'I guarantee his body (jasad)'

Key Takeaway
A kafalah bi al-nafs is valid only if the wording refers to the entire person; specifying a limb invalidates the contract.

Profit for Guarantor from Property Received Before Debt Payment
Intra-Hanafi dispute on profit from specific property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on profit from property received by a guarantor before debt payment and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding specific property.

Core Idea
Ownership vests by possession, but khubth (moral impurity) attaches to specific property, making disposal recommended but not obligatory.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah examines a nuanced question in the law of guarantee (kafalah): if the principal debtor gives property to the guarantor before the guarantor has paid the debt, and the guarantor earns profit from that property, what is the ruling? The answer differs depending on whether the property is fungible (like dirhams) or specific (like a particular quantity of wheat). The passage establishes ownership upon possession through a clever analogy to deferred debt, then presents the well-known intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the moral obligation to dispose of the profit from specific property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
First, distinguish the fungible property case (e.g., 1000 dirhams) from the specific property case (e.g., a kurr of wheat). The ruling differs due to the concept of khubth (moral impurity).
Fungible: profit is halal and pure. Specific: profit is halal but morally tainted.
2
Trace the ownership argument
Understand why the guarantor becomes owner of the property upon possession. The key analogy is to a deferred debt (dayn mu'ajjal) where early payment still transfers ownership.
The guarantor's right against the principal debtor vests at the moment of guarantee, though demand is deferred until payment.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the profit is entirely the guarantor's with no recommendation to give it away. Their proof: the profit was earned on his own property; ownership is complete and unconditional.
They see no khubth because the conditionality of the debtor's consent does not affect ownership.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's position
Imam Abu Hanifa agrees the profit is legally his, but due to khubth he recommends (istihbaban) that the profit be returned to the principal debtor or given in charity. The khubth arises because the debtor's consent was conditional on the guarantor paying the debt.
Khubth only affects specific property (mu'ayyan), not fungible.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The difference is that according to Abu Hanifa, the guarantor is morally advised to dispose of the profit (mustahabb), but it is not legally obligatory. According to the Sahibayn, there is no such recommendation. The relied-upon fatwa follows the Sahibayn in terms of legal compulsion, but the more correct view according to the commentator is Abu Hanifa's istihbab.
The ruling is mustahabb, not wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف الهدایہ جلد نم ١٨٩ كتاب الكفالة تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کفیل نے مکفول عنہ کی طرف سے مکفول لہ کو قرضہ کا مال ادا نہ کیا ہو اور مکفول عنہ نے کفیل کو قرضہ ادا کرنے کے لئے ایک ہزار درہم دیدیئے ہوں۔ پھر کفیل نے اس ایک ہزار درہم کے ذریعہ تجارت وغیرہ سے نفع حاصل کیا ہو تو یہ نفع کفیل کے لئے حلال ہوگا اور اس کا صدقہ کرنا کفیل پر واجب نہ ہوگا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ کفیل ایک ہزار درہم پر قبضہ کرنے کی وجہ سے ان کا مالک ہو گیا ہے۔ پس کفیل نے جو کچھ نفع حاصل کیا ہے اپنی ملک سے حاصل کیا ہے اور وہ نفع جو اپنی ملک سے حاصل کیا جائے چونکہ وہ حاصل کرنے والے کے لئے حلال اور طیب ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے یہ نفع بھی کفیل کے لئے حلال اور طیب ہوگا۔ رہی یہ بات کہ کفیل ایک ہزار درہم پر قبضہ کرنے کی وجہ سے مالک کیوں ہو جاتا ہے تو اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ مکفول لہ کا قرضہ کفیل ادا کرے گا یا مکفول عنہ ادا کرے گا۔ اگر مکفول لہ کا قرضہ کفیل نے ادا کیا ہے تو مکفول عنہ کے دیئے ہوئے ایک ہزار درہم پر قبضہ کرنے کی وجہ سے کفیل کا مالک ہونا ظاہر ہے کیونکہ کفیل نے اس مال پر قبضہ کیا ہے جو کفیل کا کفالہ کی وجہ سے مکفول عنہ پر واجب ہوا تھا۔ اور جو شخص ایسے مال پر قبضہ کرے جو مال اس کا دوسرے پر واجب ہو تو قبضہ کرنے والا قبضہ کرتے ہی اس مال کا مالک ہو جائے گا زیادہ سے زیادہ آپ یہ کہہ سکتے ہیں کہ کفیل نے مکفول عنہ کی طرف سے قرضہ تو بعد میں ادا کیا ہے لیکن مکفول عنہ سے پہلے ہی وصول کر لیا حالانکہ کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے رجوع کرنے کا حق ادا کرنے کے بعد ہوتا ہے نہ کہ ادا کرنے سے پہلے ۔ پس ادا کرنے سے پہلے قبضہ کرنے کی صورت میں کفیل کو مال مقبوضہ کا مالک نہ ہونا چاہئے تھا ۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ کفالہ کی وجہ سے کفیل کا مکفول عنہ پر اس کے مثل واجب تھا جو مکفول لہ کا کفیل پر واجب ہوا تھا۔ صرف اتنی بات ہے کہ مکفول لہ کو کفالہ کے فورا بعد سے مطالبہ کا حق حاصل ہو جاتا ہے اور کفیل کو مکفول عنہ کی طرف سے قرضہ ادا کرنے کے بعد یہ حق حاصل ہوتا ہے پس کفیل کے ادا کرنے سے پہلے مکفول عنہ کا کفیل کو ایک ہزار درہم دینا ایسا ہے جیسے ایک شخص کا دوسرے پر میعادی قرضہ ہو اور قرضدار نے میعاد پوری ہونے سے پہلے قرض خواہ کو قرضہ کا مال دیدیا ہو تو قرض خواہ اگر چہ میعاد پوری ہونے سے پہلے قرضہ کے مال پر قبضہ کرتا ہے لیکن اس کے باوجود قبضہ کرنے سے اس کا مالک ہو جاتا ہے پس اسی طرح ادائے قرض سے پہلے کفیل بھی اس ایک ہزار درہم کا مالک ہو جائے گا جو مکفول عنہ نے کفیل کو قرضہ ادا کرنے کے واسطے دیا ہے بہر حال اگر مکفول لہ کا قرضہ کفیل نے ادا کیا ہو تو مکفول عنہ کے دیئے ہوئے ایک ہزار درہم پر قبضہ کرنے کی وجہ سے کفیل کا مالک ہونا ظاہر ہے اور اگر مکفول لہ کا قرضہ مکفول عنہ نے ادا کیا ہو اور مکفول عنہ کو کفیل سے وہ ایک ہزار درہم واپس لینے کا حق ہو جو اس نے کفیل کو قرضہ ادا کرنے کے لئے دیا تھا تو بھی کفیل قبضہ کرتے ہی اس ایک ہزار درہم کا مالک ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ کفالہ کی وجہ سے کفیل کے لئے مکفول عنہ پر اس کے مثل مطالبہ دین واجب ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ مکفول لہ کے لئے کفیل پر واجب ہوتا ہے صرف اتنی بات ہے کہ مکفول لہ کو فی الحال مطالبہ کرنے کا حق حاصل ہے اور کفیل کو قرضہ ادا کرنے کے بعد یہ حق حاصل ہوگا یعنی کفیل مکفول عنہ سے اس وقت مطالبہ کر سکتا ہے جب مکفول لہ کو ادا کر دے لیکن اس تاخیر سے یہ لازم نہیں آتا کہ کفیل کا مکفول عنہ پر حق بھی واجب نہ ہوا ہو بلکہ حق تو کفالہ کرتے ہی واجب ہو گیا ہے صرف مطالبہ نہیں کر سکتا جیسے قرض خواہ اپنے میعادی قرضہ کافی الحال مطالبہ نہیں کر سکتا۔ پس کفیل کا مکفول عنہ پر جو حق ہے وہ دین مؤجل یعنی میعادی قرضہ کے مرتبہ میں اتار لیا گیا ہے اور میعادی قرضہ میں اگر قرضدار نے میعاد سے پہلے قرضہ دیدیا تو قرض خواہ قبضہ کرتے ہی مالک ہو جاتا ہے اسی طرح جب مکفول عنہ نے کفیل کو مطالبہ کے وقت سے پہلے دے دیا تو کفیل قبضہ کرتے ہی مالک ہو جائے گا اور چونکہ محض کفالہ کی وجہ سے کفیل کا مکفول عنہ پر مطالبہ دین واجب ہو جاتا ہے اگر چہ یہ مطالبہ ، قرض ادا کرنے تک مؤخر ہو جاتا ہے اس وجہ سے اگر کفیل نے مکفول لہ کا قرضہ ادا کرنے سے پہلے مکفول عنہ کو بری کر دیا تو یہ بری کرنا صحیح ہے۔ یعنی کفیل نے مکفول عنہ کو اپنے حق سے پہلے معاف کیا اور پھر اس کی طرف سے قرضہ ادا کیا تو یہ صحیح ہے۔ پس ادائے قرض سے پہلے کفیل کا مکفول عنہ کو اپنے حق سے بری کر دینے کا صحیح ہونا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ نفس کفالہ سے کفیل کا مکفول عنہ پر حق واجب ہو جاتا ہے اور جب نفس کفالہ سے کفیل کا مکفول عنہ پر حق واجب ہو جاتا ہے تو اگر کفیل قرضہ ادا کرنے سے پہلے اپنے اس حق پر قبضہ کرلے تو قبضہ کرنے سے اس کا مالک ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس نے اپنے حق پر قبضہ کیا ہے۔ بہر حال مکفول لہ کو کفیل قرضہ ادا کرے یا مکفول عنہ ادا کرے دونوں صورتوں میں کفیل اس ایک ہزار درہم کا مالک ہو جائے گا جو ایک ہزار مکفول عنہ نے کفیل کو قرضہ ادا کرنے کے لئے دیا ہے اور جب کفیل اس ایک ہزار درہم کا مالک ہو گیا تو اس نے جو کچھ نفع حاصل کیا ہے اپنی ملک سے حاصل کیا ہے اور جو نفع اپنی ملک سے حاصل کیا جاتا ہے وہ چونکہ حاصل کرنے والے کے لئے حلال ہوتا ہے اس لئے کفیل کے واسطے بھی مذکورہ ایک ہزار درہم سے حاصل شدہ نفع حلال اور طیب ہو گا ہاں اتنی بات ضرور ہے کہ اگر مکفول لہ کا قرضہ مکفول عنہ نے ادا کیا ہو اور کفیل نے اس ایک ہزار درہم میں تجارت کے ذریعہ نفع حاصل کیا ہو جو ایک ہزار درہم مکفول عنہ نے کفیل کو قرضہ ادا کرنے کے لئے دیئے تھے تو حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ کے مذہب کے مطابق اس نفع میں ایک گونہ خبث ہے جیسا کہ اگلے مسئلہ میں بیان کریں گے مگر یہ خبث ایسی چیز میں مؤثر نہیں ہوتا جو متعین کرنے سے متعین نہ ہوتی ہو اور اس کا مالک ہو جیسے اس مسئلہ میں ایک ہزار درہم قابل تعیین نہیں ہیں لہذا کفیل نے ان سے جو نفع حاصل کیا ہے وہ نفع اس کے واسطے حلال اور طیب ہوگا اور جو چیز متعین کرنے سے متعین ہو جاتی ہو اور اس کا مالک بھی ہو اس میں خبث مؤثر ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ اس کی تفصیل آئندہ مسئلہ میں مذکور ہے اور اس کی پوری تفصیل احکام بیع فاسد کی فصل کے تحت بھی گذر چکی ہے۔ كفيل نے ایک گر گندم کی كفالت اٹھائی اس پر قبضہ کر کے بیچ کر منافع حاصل كئے تو وہ اسی کے ہوں گے ولو كانت الكفالة بكر حنظة فقبضها الكفيل فباعها و ربح فيها فالربح له فى الحكم لما بينا انه ملكه قال و احب الى أن يردّه على الذي قضاه الكر ولا يجب عليه فى الحكم وهذا عند أبي حنيفة في رواية الجامع الصغير وقال ابو يوسف و محمد هو له ولا يرده على الذى قضاه و هو رواية عنه وعنه انه يتصدق به لهما انه ربح في ملكه على الوجه الذى بيناه فيسلم له وله انه تمكن الخبث مع الملك اما لانه بسبيل من الاسترداد بان يقضيه بنفسه اولانه رضی به علی اعتبار قضاء الكفيل فاذا قضاه بنفسه لم يكن راضيا به و هذا الخبث يعمل فيما يتعين فيكون سبيله التصدق فى رواية و يرده عليه فى رواية لان الخبث لحقه وهذا اصح لكنه استحباب لا جبر لان الحق له ترجمہ اور اگر ایک گر گندم کا کفالہ ہو پھر اس پر کفیل نے قبضہ کر کے اس کو فروخت کیا۔ اور اس میں نفع حاصل کیا تو یہ نفع قضا کفیل کے واسطے ہو گا اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی کہ کفیل اس کا مالک ہو گیا ہے امام ابو حنیفہ نے کہا کہ مجھے یہ بات پسند ہے کہ یہ نفع اسی شخص کو واپس کر دے جس نے اس کو ایک کر گندم دیا تھا لیکن حکما اس پر واپس کرنا واجب نہیں ہے۔ یہ حکم ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک جامع صغیر کی روایت میں مذکور ہے اور امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ وہ نفع کفیل کے واسطے ہے لہذا اس کو اس شخص پر واپس بھی نہ کرے جس نے
Ashraf al-Hidaya Volume 9, page 189. Chapter of Kafala. Explanation of the scenario: If the guarantor has not paid the debt to the creditor on behalf of the principal debtor, and the principal debtor gave the guarantor one thousand dirhams to pay the debt, then the guarantor made profit through trade etc. with that one thousand dirhams, then this profit is permissible for the guarantor and it is not obligatory for him to give it in charity. The proof is that the guarantor became the owner of the one thousand dirhams by taking possession. So the profit he made is from his own property, and profit from one's own property is permissible and pure. Therefore this profit is also permissible and pure for the guarantor. As for why the guarantor becomes the owner by taking possession: the debt to the creditor will be paid either by the guarantor or the principal debtor. If the guarantor paid the debt to the creditor, then his ownership of the one thousand dirhams given by the principal debtor is clear because he took possession of wealth that was owed to him by the principal debtor due to the guarantee. And whoever takes possession of wealth that is owed to him becomes its owner immediately. At most you can say that the guarantor paid the debt later but collected before payment, whereas his right to recourse arises only after payment, not before. So in the case of taking possession before payment, the guarantor should not be the owner of the possessed wealth. The answer is that by the guarantee, the guarantor had a claim against the principal debtor similar to what the creditor had against the guarantor. The only difference is that the creditor has the right to demand immediately after the guarantee, while the guarantor has this right after paying the debt. So the principal debtor giving one thousand dirhams to the guarantor before payment is like a person who has a deferred debt and the debtor pays before the term; the creditor becomes owner by taking possession despite the early payment. Similarly, the guarantor becomes owner of the one thousand dirhams given by the principal debtor for payment. In any case, if the guarantor paid the debt, his ownership is clear. If the principal debtor paid the debt and the principal debtor has the right to take back the one thousand dirhams he gave, still the guarantor becomes owner upon taking possession, because by the guarantee the guarantor has a claim against the principal debtor similar to the creditor's claim against the guarantor, only the timing of demand differs. The delay does not mean the right did not become due; it became due at the time of guarantee, but demand is postponed like a deferred debt. So the guarantor's right is like a deferred debt. In a deferred debt, if the debtor pays early, the creditor becomes owner upon possession. Similarly, when the principal debtor gave before the time of demand, the guarantor becomes owner upon possession. And because by the mere guarantee the guarantor has a claim against the principal debtor, even if postponed until payment, if the guarantor discharges the principal debtor from this right before paying the debt, it is valid. This shows that the right becomes due by the guarantee itself. So if the guarantor takes possession of his right before payment, he becomes owner. In both cases (whether the guarantor pays or the principal debtor pays), the guarantor becomes owner of the one thousand dirhams given by the principal debtor. And when he becomes owner, profit from it is his own property, and profit from one's own property is permissible and pure. So the profit is permissible and pure for the guarantor. However, if the principal debtor paid the debt and the guarantor made profit from the one thousand dirhams given for payment, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa there is some degree of impurity (khubth) in this profit, as will be explained in the next issue. But this impurity does not affect something that is not determined by specification and is owned, like in this case where one thousand dirhams are not determinable. So the profit from them is permissible and pure. But if the item is determined by specification and is owned, then the impurity affects it, as detailed in the next issue and also previously in the chapter on invalid sales. If the guarantee was for a kurr of wheat, and the guarantor took possession, sold it, and made profit, then in legal ruling the profit is his, as we explained that he owns it. He (Abu Hanifa) said: I prefer that he return it to the one who paid the kurr, but it is not obligatory upon him in legal ruling. This is according to Abu Hanifa in a narration from al-Jami' al-Saghir. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: It is his and he does not return it to the one who paid, and there is a narration from him (Abu Hanifa) that he gives it in charity. For them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): He made profit on his property in the manner we explained, so it belongs to him. For him (Abu Hanifa): Impurity (khubth) is attached along with ownership, either because it is subject to reclaim (by the principal debtor paying the debt himself), or because he (the principal debtor) consented to it on the condition that the guarantor pays, so if he pays himself, he is not pleased with it. And this impurity takes effect in what is determined, so its way is either charity in one narration or return in another, because impurity has attached to it. This is more correct, but it is recommended, not compulsory, because the right is his. Translation: And if the guarantee was for a kurr of wheat, then the guarantor took possession, sold it, and made profit, then in legal ruling the profit is his, due to the proof we mentioned that he became its owner. Imam Abu Hanifa said: I prefer that he return this profit to the person who gave him the kurr of wheat, but it is not obligatory upon him. This ruling is according to Abu Hanifa in the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir. Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad said: The profit is for the guarantor, so he should not return it to the person who gave.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is a detailed legal ruling (intra-Hanafi dispute) on the permissibility of profit earned by a guarantor (kafil) from property received from the principal debtor (makful anhu) before the guarantor has paid the debt to the creditor (makful lahu). The author, while commenting on the Hidayah, explains the legal reasoning and the points of difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). The passage consists of two main parts: first, a general ruling on non-specific fungible property (like dirhams), and second, a specific ruling on a specific quantity (a kurr of wheat). In the first part, the ruling is unanimous that the profit is halal and pure for the guarantor because he becomes the owner of the property upon possession. The reasoning establishes that the guarantor has a right against the principal debtor from the moment of the guarantee contract, even though the right to demand payment is deferred until after the guarantor pays the creditor. This is analogized to a deferred debt (dayn mu'ajjal): if the debtor pays early, the creditor becomes owner. Similarly, when the principal debtor gives property to the guarantor before the guarantor's payment, the guarantor becomes owner. Evidence for the early vesting of the right is that the guarantor can validly discharge the principal debtor from this right before paying the creditor, which would be impossible if the right did not exist. In the second part, for a specific determinable item like a kurr of wheat, Imam Abu Hanifa holds that although the guarantor becomes owner and the profit is legally his, there is a degree of impurity (khubth) because the principal debtor's payment was on the assumption that the guarantor would pay the debt; if the principal debtor ends up paying himself, he may not have consented to the guarantor using the wheat for profit. Therefore, Abu Hanifa recommends (istihbaban) that the guarantor either return the profit or give it in charity, but it is not legally obligatory. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the profit is purely the guarantor's, without any recommendation of disposal, because the profit was generated on his own property. The text notes that khubth only affects items that are determinate by specification (mu'ayyan). This distinction reflects the Hanafi principle that in fungible (ghayr mu'ayyan) property, the element of khubth does not nullify the permissibility, while in specific property, it may create a moral recommendation.

Key Terms
كفالة (kafālah): A contract of guarantee or suretyship where a person (kafil) undertakes to fulfill an obligation of another (makful anhu) to a third party (makful lahu).
كفيل (kafīl): The guarantor who undertakes to pay the debt if the principal debtor fails.
مكفول عنه (makfūl ‘anhu): The principal debtor on whose behalf the guarantee is given.
مكفول له (makfūl lahu): The creditor who is the beneficiary of the guarantee.
خبث (khubth): Moral impurity or undesirability attached to profit due to the possibility that the principal debtor's consent was conditional on the guarantor paying the debt.
دين مؤجل (dayn mu’ajjal): A deferred debt with a fixed future payment date. Used here as an analogy for the guarantor's right against the principal debtor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on profit earned by a guarantor from a specific quantity of wheat (e.g., a kurr) received before paying the debt, according to the preferred view (hadha asahh)?
A) The profit is forbidden and must be given in charity.
B) The profit is halal, but it is recommended to return it or give it in charity, though not obligatory.
C) The profit is halal and the guarantor may keep it with no recommendation.
D) The profit must be returned to the principal debtor immediately.

Key Takeaway
For specific property received by a guarantor before paying the debt, the profit is legally the guarantor's, but it is recommended (mustahabb) to dispose of it due to moral impurity (khubth), though no legal obligation exists.

Acceptance of Evidence When Guarantee is Conditional
Explains why bayyinah is not accepted when kafala is conditional.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a creditor's evidence is not accepted against a conditional guarantor and apply the principle of mutabaqat to assess claim validity.

Core Idea
Claim and guarantee must match; mismatch invalidates claim and rejects evidence.

In this passage, the commentary clarifies a key procedural rule in Hanafi kafala. When a guarantee is phrased conditionally—e.g., 'whatever is decreed'—the guaranteed debt is restricted. If the creditor then claims an absolute amount without linking it to that condition, the claim lacks correspondence (mutabaqat) with the guarantee. This lack of correspondence makes the claim invalid, and therefore the creditor's evidence is not accepted. The ruling hinges on the principle that evidence is only accepted for a valid claim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the guarantee's wording
Note the conditional phrasing: 'ma qudiya' or 'ma dhaba' indicates the guarantee is restricted to a debt that was or will be decreed.
The past tense may refer to future acts.
2
Compare the creditor's claim
The creditor claims an absolute amount (e.g., 1000 dirhams) without mentioning any condition or decree.
Absolute (mutlaq) vs. restricted (muqayyad).
3
Apply the mutabaqat requirement
For a claim to be valid, its subject must correspond exactly to the guaranteed debt.
Mutabaqat is a condition for sahhal-da'wa.
4
Check for correspondence
Here, the guarantee is restricted to a decreed debt, but the claim is not so restricted; they do not match.
No correspondence = claim invalid.
5
Determine the consequence
Since the claim is invalid, the evidence (bayyinah) is not accepted unless the principal debtor appears.
Exception: when principal debtor is present, evidence may be accepted.

کفیل ہوں جس کا فلاں کے لئے اس پر فیصلہ کیا گیا ہو۔ پھر مکفول عنہ غائب ہو گیا اور مدعی یعنی مکفول لہ نے کفیل پر گواہ پیش کئے کہ میرا مکفول عنہ پر ایک ہزار درہم ہے تو مکفول لہ کے گواہ قبول نہ ہوں گے۔ یعنی حامد غائب ہو گیا اور مکفول لہ یعنی شاہد نے کفیل یعنی خالد پر بعینہ پیش کیا کہ میرے مکفول عنہ یعنی حامد پر ایک ہزار درہم ہیں تو مکفول لہ یعنی شاہد کا بینہ قبول نہ ہو گا۔ البتہ مکفول عنہ کے حاضر ہونے پر مکفول لہ کا بینہ قبول کر لیا جائیگا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ بینہ کا قبول ہونا صحت دعویٰ پر موقوف ہے یعنی اگر دعویٰ صحیح ہے تو مدعی کا بینہ قبول ہوگا ورنہ نہیں اور یہاں مکفول لہ کا دعویٰ صحیح نہیں ہے کیونکہ دعویٰ اور مکفول بہ کے درمیان مطابقت موجود نہیں ہے حالانکہ اس جگہ صحت دعویٰ کے لئے دعویٰ اور مکفول بہ کے درمیان مطابقت کا ہونا ضروری ہے اور مکفول بہ اور دعویٰ میں مطابقت اس لئے موجود نہیں ہے کہ مال مکفول بہ یا تو وہ مال ہے جس کا کفالہ سے پہلے مکفول عنہ پر حکم کر دیا گیا ہے کیونکہ کفیل نے ما قضی ماضی کا صیغہ ذکر کیا ہے جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ کفالہ سے پہلے جس مال کا مکفول عنہ پر قاضی نے حکم کیا ہے کفیل نے اس کی کفالت کی ہے اور ما ذاب له علیه کہنے کی صورت میں بھی مکفول بہ وہ مال ہے جس کا کفالہ سے پہلے مکفول عنہ پر حکم کیا گیا ہے کیونکہ ذاب کے معنی تقرر اور وجوب کے ہیں اور تقرر مال قضائے قاضی سے ہوتا ہے پس ثابت ہوا کہ کفیل نے اس مال کی کفالت کی ہے جو قضائے قاضی سے واجب ہوا ہے یا مال مکفول بہ وہ مال ہے جس کا کفالہ کے بعد مکفول عنہ پر حکم کیا جائے گا کیونکہ لفظ ذاب اور قضی اگر چہ صیغہ ماضی ہیں لیکن مراد مستقبل ہے جیسے اطال الله بقائک میں لفظ اطال ماضی ہے لیکن استقبال کے معنی مراد ہیں بہر حال مکفول بہ وہ مال ہو جس کا مکفول عنہ پر کفالہ سے پہلے حکم کر دیا گیا ہے یا وہ مال ہو جس کا کفالہ کے بعد حکم کیا جائے گا دونوں صورتوں میں مکفول بہ مال مقید ہے اور مکفول لہ کا مکفول عنہ پر ایک ہزار درہم کا دعویٰ مطلق ہے یعنی مکفول لہ نے مطلقاً ایک ہزار درہم کا دعویٰ کیا ہے۔ دعویٰ میں نہ اس سے تعرض کیا کہ کفالہ سے پہلے مکفول عنہ پر اس کا حکم کیا گیا ہو اور نہ اس بات سے تعرض کیا کہ کفالہ کے بعد حکم کیا جائے گا پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ مال مکفول بہ اور دعویٰ کے درمیان مطابقت نہیں ہے اور جب دعویٰ اور مال مکفول بہ کے درمیان مطابقت نہیں پائی گئی تو دعویٰ صحیح نہ ہوگا اور جب دعویٰ صحیح نہیں ہوا تو بعینہ بھی قبول نہ ہوگا۔
Explanation of the case: A person becomes a guarantor for another with these words: 'Whatever is established against him, i.e., whatever comes out in accounting, I am the guarantor for it,' or he said, 'I am the guarantor for that right which has been decreed for so-and-so against him.' Then the principal debtor becomes absent, and the plaintiff (the creditor) brings witnesses against the guarantor that the principal debtor owes him one thousand dirhams. Then the creditor's witnesses will not be accepted. For example, Khalid said, 'I am the guarantor on behalf of Hamid for that wealth which is established for Shahid against Hamid,' or Khalid said, 'I am the guarantor on behalf of Hamid for that right which will be decreed for Shahid against him.' Then the principal debtor, Hamid, becomes absent, and the creditor, Shahid, presents evidence against the guarantor, Khalid, that his principal debtor, Hamid, owes him one thousand dirhams. Then Shahid's evidence will not be accepted. However, upon the presence of the principal debtor, the creditor's evidence will be accepted. The proof is that acceptance of evidence depends on the validity of the claim. That is, if the claim is valid, the plaintiff's evidence is accepted; otherwise, not. And here the creditor's claim is not valid because there is no correspondence between the claim and the guaranteed debt. In this case, for the validity of the claim, correspondence between the claim and the guaranteed debt is necessary. Correspondence does not exist because the guaranteed debt is either that wealth which was decreed against the principal debtor before the suretyship, since the guarantor mentioned the past tense 'ma qudiya' meaning that the guarantor guaranteed that wealth which the judge had decreed against the principal debtor before the suretyship. Similarly, in case of saying 'ma dhaba lahu alayhi' the guaranteed debt is that wealth which was decreed against the principal debtor before the suretyship, because 'dhaba' means established and obligatory, and establishment of wealth occurs by the judge's decree. Thus it is established that the guarantor guaranteed that wealth which became obligatory by the judge's decree. Or the guaranteed debt is that wealth which will be decreed against the principal debtor after the suretyship, because the words 'dhaba' and 'qudiya' are past tense but intended for the future, like 'ataalla allahu baqa'aka' where 'ataala' is past tense but means future. In any case, the guaranteed debt is either that wealth which was decreed before the suretyship or that which will be decreed after. In both cases, the guaranteed debt is restricted, while the creditor's claim against the principal debtor of one thousand dirhams is absolute. That is, the creditor claimed one thousand dirhams absolutely, without specifying that it was decreed before or after the suretyship. Thus it is established that there is no correspondence between the guaranteed debt and the claim. Since there is no correspondence between the claim and the guaranteed debt, the claim is not valid, and when the claim is not valid, the evidence is not accepted.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling-with-proof from the commentary Ashraf al-Hidayah. It explains that when a guarantor (kafil) uses conditional language—such as 'whatever is established' or 'whatever is decreed'—the guaranteed debt is restricted (muqayyad) to that specific debt that was or will be decreed by a judge. In contrast, the creditor's claim is absolute (mutlaq), stating a fixed amount without reference to any such condition. For a claim to be valid (sahih), the subject matter of the claim must match the subject matter of the guarantee (mutabaqat). Here, since the guarantee is conditional and the claim is absolute, they do not correspond, so the claim is invalid. Consequently, the creditor's evidence (bayyinah) is not accepted unless the principal debtor (makful anhu) is present and confirms the debt. The proof is based on the legal principle that acceptance of evidence is contingent on the validity of the claim. This is a rational (aqli) proof, not directly from Quran or Sunnah, but grounded in the structure of judicial procedure. The Hanafi position is that the claim must be specific and correspond to what is guaranteed.

Key Terms
مکفول بہ (makful bihi): The debt or property that is the subject of the suretyship.
مطابقت (mutabaqat): Correspondence or matching between the claim (da'wa) and the subject matter of the guarantee (makful bihi).
قضی (qudiya): Past tense of 'to decree' but can be used for future events (istighbal).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the lesson, why is the creditor's evidence not accepted against the guarantor?
A) Because the guarantor is absent.
B) Because the claim is absolute while the guarantee is conditional, causing lack of correspondence.
C) Because the debt is less than ten dirhams.
D) Because the guarantor denied the debt.

Key Takeaway
A conditional guarantee requires the claim to match the condition; otherwise evidence is rejected until the principal debtor appears.

Kafala bi-Amri vs bi-Ghayri Amri: Judgment and Recourse
Intra-Hanafi dispute on kafala judgment and recourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between kafala bi-amri and bi-ghayri amri in terms of judgment effect and the guarantor's right of recourse, and apply the Hanafi position in a dispute about the guarantor's denial of the order.

Core Idea
With order, judgment binds both; without order, only the guarantor. Recourse follows the same distinction.

This passage delves into the nuances of suretyship (kafala) by examining two fundamental types: those undertaken with the principal debtor's order and those without. The distinction carries significant legal consequences for the effect of a court judgment and the guarantor's ability to reclaim paid amounts from the debtor. We will also explore an intra-Hanafi disagreement concerning the guarantor's right to recourse when he initially denies that the suretyship was with the debtor's order.

Guided Path
1
Distinguishing the two types of kafala
Identify the two categories: kafala bi-amrihi (with the debtor's order) and kafala bi-ghayri amrihi (without). Note that in the first, the act is a donation initially but becomes a compensated transaction eventually; in the second, it is a pure donation both initially and eventually.
2
Tracing the effect on the judgment
Understand that when the guaranteed debt is absolute (mutlaq) and the creditor's claim is also absolute, the evidence is accepted in both types. However, the judgment's effect differs: with order, it binds both the guarantor and the absent principal debtor; without order, it binds only the guarantor. Reason: kafala bi-amri implies the principal's order and acknowledgment of the debt.
3
Analyzing the guarantor's right of recourse
Note the general rule: in kafala bi-amri, the guarantor can recover from the principal debtor; in kafala bi-ghayri amri, he cannot. Then examine the intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Zufar argues that if the guarantor initially denied the suretyship (e.g., claimed it was without order), he cannot later claim recourse because he would be contradicting his own claim of oppression.
4
Applying the Hanafi response
The majority Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) holds that the guarantor's denial is rejected by the Shari'a once the court establishes the order through evidence. Therefore, the denial is nullified, and he retains the right to recourse. The court's judgment overrides his earlier claim.
The key is that the guarantor is not considered oppressed; rather, his denial is deemed false.
5
Identifying the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In practice, if a guarantor pays the debt and then sues the principal debtor for reimbursement, the court will allow it if the suretyship was with order, even if the guarantor had earlier denied having an order. Under Zufar's view, the guarantor would lose this right.

Source Text

کسی نے مبینہ قائم کر دیئے کہ میرا فلاں پر اس قدر مال ہے اور یہ شخص اس کی طرف سے اس کے حکم سے کفیل ہے تو مال کا حکم کفیل اور مکفول عنہ پر دیدیا جائے گا۔ اور اگر کفالہ بغیر اس کے حکم کے ہو تو خاص طور سے کفیل پر حکم کیا جائے گا اور بینہ اس لئے قبول کیا جائے گا کہ مکفول به مال مطلق ہے بر خلاف سابق کے۔ اور حکم ہونے اور نہ ہونے سے اختلاف اس وجہ سے ہے کہ یہ دونوں باہم مختلفان ہیں کیونکہ کفالہ بامر ابتداء تتبرع ہے اور انتهاء معاوضہ ہے اور کفالہ بغیر امر ابتداء اور انتہاء تبرع ہے۔ پس اس کے ان دونوں میں سے ایک کا دعویٰ کرنے کی وجہ سے اس کے واسطے دوسری قسم کا فیصلہ نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ اور جب کفالہ بالا مر کا حکم دیدیا گیا تو مکفول عنہ کا حکم دینا ثابت ہو گیا اور یہ مال کے اقرار کو بھی متضمن ہے ہیں یہ اقرار بھی مکفول عنہ پر حکم کیا ہوا ہو جائے گا۔ اور کفالہ بغیر امرہ مکفول عنہ کی جانب کو نہیں لگتا۔ کیونکہ صحت کفالہ کفیل کے گمان میں قیام دین پر موقوف ہے لہذا دین مکفول عنہ کی طرف متعدی نہ ہوگا۔ اور کفالہ بامر میں کفیل ادا کیا ہوا مال مکفول عنہ سے واپس لے گا۔ اور امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ واپس نہیں لے گا کیونکہ جب کفیل نے کفالہ کا انکار کیا تو وہ اپنے گمان میں مظلوم ہوا۔ پس وہ اپنے علاوہ پر ظلم نہیں کرے گا۔ اور ہم کہتے ہیں کہ کفیل مذکور کی شرعا تکذیب کر دی گئی ہے تو جو کچھ کفیل کے گمان میں تھی وہ باطل ہو گیا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ایک شخص مثل حامد، خالد کی طرف سے اس کے حکم سے مال مؤجل کا کفیل ہو گیا پھر مکفول عنہ یعنی خالد غائب ہو گیا پھر مکفول لہ یعنی شاہد نے قاضی کی عدالت میں دعویٰ کر کے بینہ پیش کیا کہ میرا فلاں غائب یعنی خالد پر اس قدر مال ہے اور یہ یعنی حامد اس کی طرف سے اس کے حکم سے کفیل ہے تو مذکورہ مال کے سلسلہ میں قاضی کا یہ فیصلہ کفیل اور مکفول عنہ دونوں پر نافذ ہوگا یعنی کفیل حاضر پر جو حکم کیا جائے گا اس کے ذیل میں مکفول عنہ غائب پر بھی حکم ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر کفالہ، مکفول عنہ کے حکم سے نہ ہو تو مکفول لہ کے بینہ کی وجہ سے مال کا حکم فقط کفیل پر کیا جائے گا مکفول عنہ غائب پر قاضی کا یہ حکم نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ حاصل یہ کہ اس مسئلہ میں کفالہ بامرہ ہو یا کفالہ بغیر امرہ ہو دونوں صورتوں میں مکفول لہ کا بینہ قبول کر لیا جائے گا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس مسئلہ میں مکفول بہ مال مطلق ہے کیونکہ کفیل نے اس مال کو نہ تو ما قضی (جس کا حکم کر دیا گیا) کے ساتھ مقید کیا ہے اور نہ یقضی بہ (جس کا فیصلہ کیا جائے گا) کے ساتھ مقید کیا ہے اور جب کسی قید کے ساتھ مقید نہیں کیا تو مکفول بہ مال مطلق ہوا اور مکفول لہ کا دعویٰ بھی مطلق ہے کیونکہ مکفول لہ نے یہ دعویٰ کیا ہے کہ میرا مکفول عنہ پر اس قدر مال ہے اور اس مال کو کسی قید کے ساتھ مقید نہیں کیا ہے۔ پس جب دعویٰ اور مدعی بہ (مال مکفول بہ) دونوں مطلق ہیں تو مطابقت کے پائے جانی کی وجہ سے دعویٰ صحیح ہوگا۔ اور جب دعویٰ صحیح ہے تو بینہ بھی قبول کر لیا جائے گا کیونکہ جو بعینہ، دعویٰ صحیح پر مبنی ہوتا ہے اس کو شرعا قبول کیا جاتا ہے لہذا اس مسئلہ میں بھی مکفول لہ کا پیش کردہ بینہ قبول کر لیا جائے گا۔ اس کے برخلاف گذشتہ مسئلہ میں کہ اس میں دعویٰ اور مدعی بہ (مکفول بہ) کے درمیان مطابقت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے بینہ قبول نہ ہوگا۔
Whoever establishes evidence that so-and-so owes him a certain amount and that this person is a guarantor for him by his order, then the judgment will be passed on both the guarantor and the principal debtor. And if the suretyship is without his order, then the judgment will be passed specifically on the guarantor. And the evidence is accepted because the guaranteed debt is absolute (mutlaq), contrary to the previous. And the difference between with order and without order is because they are different: kafala bi-amri is a donation initially but a compensation eventually, while kafala bi-ghayri amri is a donation both initially and eventually. So if a claim is made for one of these two types, judgment cannot be given for the other. And when judgment is given for kafala bi-amri, the order of the principal debtor is established, and it also entails acknowledgment of the debt, so that acknowledgment becomes a judgment against the principal debtor. Kafala bi-ghayri amri does not affect the principal debtor because the validity of the suretyship in the guarantor's presumption is dependent on the existence of the debt; therefore the debt does not extend to the principal debtor. In kafala bi-amri, the guarantor will recover what he paid from the principal debtor. Imam Zufar said he will not recover, because when the guarantor denied the suretyship, he became oppressed in his presumption, so he will not oppress others. But we say that the mentioned guarantor is deemed a liar by the Shari'a, so whatever was in his presumption is nullified. Explanation of the case: If a person, like Hamid, becomes a guarantor on behalf of Khalid, by his order, for a deferred debt, then the principal debtor Khalid becomes absent, then the creditor Shahid claims in the qadi's court and presents evidence that the absent Khalid owes him a certain amount and that Hamid is the guarantor for him by his order, then the qadi's judgment regarding that money will be effective against both the guarantor and the principal debtor. That is, the judgment passed on the present guarantor will also cover the absent principal debtor. If the suretyship was not by the principal debtor's order, then due to the creditor's evidence, the judgment will be passed only on the guarantor; it will not be effective against the absent principal debtor. The gist is that in this case, whether kafala is bi-amri or bi-ghayri amri, the creditor's evidence is accepted in both. The proof is that in this case, the guaranteed debt is absolute because the guarantor did not restrict it with 'ma qudiya' (what was decreed) or 'ma yuqda bihi' (what will be decreed). When no restriction is made, the guaranteed debt is absolute, and the creditor's claim is also absolute because the creditor claimed that the principal debtor owes him a certain amount without any restriction. So when both the claim and the subject matter (guaranteed debt) are absolute, the claim is valid due to correspondence. And when the claim is valid, the evidence is accepted because bayyinah is based on a valid claim and is accepted by the Shari'a. Therefore, in this case, the evidence presented by the creditor is accepted, contrary to the previous case where evidence was rejected due to lack of correspondence between the claim and the subject matter.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute analysis concerning kafala. It distinguishes two types: kafala bi-amrihi (with the principal debtor's order) and kafala bi-ghayri amrihi (without order). In both, because the guaranteed debt is absolute (mutlaq) and the claim is absolute, the creditor's evidence is accepted. However, the effect of the judgment differs: with order, judgment binds both the guarantor and the absent principal debtor; without order, it binds only the guarantor. The reasoning is that kafala bi-amri is a donation initially but a compensation eventually (since the guarantor can recover from the principal), while without order it is a pure donation. Therefore, the judgment with order implies the principal's order and acknowledgment of debt, so it affects him. Without order, the guarantee is independent of the principal's side. Additionally, there is a dispute with Imam Zufar regarding the guarantor's right to recourse: if the guarantor denied the suretyship (e.g., claimed it was without order), can he still recover from the principal? The Hanafi position is that since the Shari'a deems him a liar (he denied the order but it was proven), his denial is rejected, and he retains the right to recourse. Zufar argues that his denial nullifies his right because he claimed to be oppressed. The proof for accepting evidence is aqli: the correspondence between absolute claim and absolute guarantee makes the claim valid, and valid claim supports evidence.

Key Terms
کفالہ بامرہ (kafala bi-amrihi): Suretyship with the prior order or permission of the principal debtor.
کفالہ بغیر امرہ (kafala bi-ghayri amrihi): Suretyship without the prior order or permission of the principal debtor.
تبرع (tabarru'): A gratuitous act, a donation without expectation of compensation.
مطلق (mutlaq): Absolute, unrestricted. In this context, a debt that is not qualified by a condition like 'already decreed' or 'to be decreed'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the effect of judgment in kafala bi-ghayri amri?
A) Judgment binds both the guarantor and the principal debtor.
B) Judgment binds only the guarantor, not the principal debtor.
C) Judgment binds only the principal debtor, not the guarantor.
D) Judgment is not passed at all because evidence is rejected.

Key Takeaway
The distinction between kafala bi-amri and bi-ghayri amri determines both the scope of the court's judgment and the guarantor's right of recourse; the majority Hanafi view allows recourse even if the guarantor initially denies the order.
